My entire family loves these cookies.  My family begs for them!  I would suggest using 4 TBsp of cocoa, butter rather than margarine, smooth PB and 3 1/2 cups of oats.  Small changes but they make a world of difference. I have tried every which way and this is the best.  If you do it just right, they set up in about 15 minutes.

text:
I've been having issues with these not turning out too! I have a different version of "rolling boil" every time I do it. According to the blog All in Good Food he decreases the sugar to 1 and 3/4 cup *this effects the sugar concentration* and brings to 230 degrees F under med-high heat. Just like fudge, if it's raining or humid, you will need to boil a bit longer (but not above max soft ball stage) so the cookie will suck moisture out of the air. Have all your ingredients pre-measured b/c this moves fast after removing from heat.

text:
This recipe is messed up. I went digging in my closet to find my orginal no-bake cookie recipe. When I compared the two recipes, I found that they had the same ingredients; however, the ratios and the cooking processes were different. The oatmeal has to be added before the peanut butter because the peanut butter cools the mixture down. If you don't, your oatmeal stays firm. The desired texture for these cookies is a slighty softened oatmeal. I would look for another recipe if you prefer a more original style no-bake  cookie. I hope this helps.

I give this five stars because they came out exactly as they were meant to.  Following the advice of other posters I doubled the cocoa (used good quality cocoa), used creamy PB, and even reduced the butter a bit.  Boiled for about 90 seconds.  They set up perfectly and were ready to eat in LESS than an hour.  I love making these when I need a quicky fudgey chocolate fix.  Oh forgot... I used 2 1/2 cups of oats and 1 cup of coconut.  I think it would be good with just the 3 cups of oats too.

text:
I thought 2 cups was a lot of sugar, so I made it 1 1/2 cups and they were plenty sweet. I doubled the cocoa (per reviews) and used 1/4 cup butter and made milk 3/4 cup to compensate for the missing liquid.  I also used reduced fat peanut butter.  They ended up with a fudgy, slightly sticky texture but I wasn't sure what the original texture should be so I don't know if my reduction of butter did that.  The only bad thing was they had a kind of raw oatmeal flavor but I didn't mind. In the end, they curbed my sweet, chocolate craving and were a little healthy to boot. I would make them again for the same reason.

I've made these often, but due to my son having a peanut allergy I replace the peanut butter with sunflower butter.  It's a bit pricey, and hard to find, but taste delicious!  It's a peanut butter substitute that is made with ground up sunflower seeds. It also worked perfect in this recipe since it looks just like peanut butter and has the exact same consistency!  Just thought I'd let other people know that they can enjoy these yummy cookies even if they are allergic to peanuts.  Yummy for the whole family!

text:
I grew up on this cookie, so making them always zips me right back to my childhood. Mom has been gone for years, and this year my sister asked me to make some for Thanksgiving; they were gone in no time! The thing to remember with these cookies is that you are basically making fudge with oatmeal in it. Having it come to the FULL boil, and letting it boil long enough, are crucial to them setting up properly. If you're in doubt you've cooked it long enough, use a candy thermometer and make sure you're in the 235-240 ballpark and you should be fine. Enjoy!!

text:
My mom has been making this for decades, and taught me when I was a little kid.  It's GREAT, and a staple in our family!  

Although I have to disagree with Sue who posted a review a few slots down - you DO need to boil it for one full minute, or it will not harden!

I've made it several times where I didn't boil for a full minute, just brought it to a boil, and it never hardened.  Over the last 15 years or so, I've made it close to a hundred times - boil it for at LEAST a full minute for it to harden properly.  

Thanks for posting!

text:
Easy as 123...these turned out FAB.  Only reason I rated a 4 is because I made adjustments. Took advise of other folks and did the following added my modifications.  MAKE SURE EVERYTHING IS PREMEASURED AND IN SEPARATE CONTAINERS SET KITCHEN TIMER TO ONE MIN BUT DONT TURN ON JUST YET. Put milk and butter in pan turn on heat, add cocoa (4tbs) then add sugar. CONSTANTELY stir at all times mixure will come to a rolling boil even while stirring.  Once rolling boil starts TURN ON TIMER.  Keep stirring until timer goes off.  Take pot off heat add salt, then vanilla (9 teaspoons= shot glass full) keep stirring add peanut butter (I did creamy) keep stirring then add oats.  Stirring mixure until completely mixed.  FINETO!  Me and my son could not get them on the wax paper as we were too busy eating from the spoon!  FAB FAB FAB!

None
text:
This recipe has been a favorite in my family my whole entire life. The secrets include having all ingredients pre-measured, using 4 tbsp of butter and remember that you have to have your cocoa mixture at a rolling boil (that means that even though you are stirring the mix, it is STILL boiling rapidly. THEN, you start your timing -- we go 5 minutes) And we use creamy peanut butter, not chunky (not everyone likes nuts) dump the oats a cup at a time, sometimes you need 3 cups, sometimes 3.5 cups oats.
Sometimes if the weather isn't the best, the cookies won't set up. They're a mess, but we eat them anyway, and have dubbed them "Mess Cookies" - the best!

text:
I followed the ingredients list exactly, and made sure that I boiled the cocoa mixture ( a full rolling boil) for about 1 and 1/2 minutes. I guess I'll have to try again, because the final result was so dry and crumbly that there was no way to spoon these out - I had to squeeze teaspoon- full amounts of the mixture together with my hands, and pray that the mixture will hold together in some sort of shape. They're cooling now, so I'm hoping the end result will not be too crumbly to eat. Very disappointed, because the ones I remember from my childhood could be spooned out onto waxed paper. I rated 4 stars because it must have been something I did wrong !
UPDATE:  I made this exact recipe again, except I used 2 and 1/2 cups of oats....turned out perfect. I'm certain that I mixed the first batch according to the recipe, so my advice to others would be to start with less oats and add more if needed. I have noticed other reviews here where other people actually used MORE oats; I have no explanation for that. It's true that you don't want them runny when you spoon them out, but my first batch was too dry !

text:
I love this recipe because it's fast, easy and there is no fuss in making them. Make sure to bring the sugar/butter/milk/cocoa to a FULL,ROLLING BOIL for exactly 1 minute, or the cookies will be mushy and the shape will not hold. Either smooth or chunky PB works well - I prefer smooth. MY ADDITIONS: added 1/2 c. more oatmeal (to avoid mushiness), milled or whole flax seed is great for more nutritional value, and for added flavor I throw in 1/2 c. coconut. Yum!

This is the exact same recipe I was given in my 6th grade home economics class and I've been making them ever since...without giving away my age I'll just say that's been a long time.  I would say the one most important thing about this recipe is to boil the ingredients for exactly one minute. Sometimes I use all of one or the other and sometimes I'll add a little less oats and throw in some coconut.  A great, easy recipe.

text:
Beautiful, simple.  This is a perfect recipe as is.
UPDATE:  Make it easy on yourself.  This is what I did.  Instead of spooning these cookies out, pour them.  Line a baking sheet with parchment or waxed paper, and pour the whole pan onto the baking sheet.  Let them cool 10-15 minutes, and then score them with a table knife into squares...whatever size you like.  Then, pop them in the fridge for a bit.  When they are completely cooled, break them into pieces and pull off the paper.  Store as you normally would.  Hope this helps make your holiday cooking a little simpler! ;)

text:
These cookies are pretty good if you're in the mood for something sweet and don't feel like baking. My son asks for them often. My recipe is very similar. The only differences are: no salt and only 1/4c. of creamy peanut butter. The biggest difference (and the real trick to getting them to set up) is to bring your butter, sugar cocoa, milk mixture to a full boil and continue to boil for exactly 3 minutes. Works every time!

text:
I, too, have been making these cookies since I was a very little girl, and have loved them all my life. I have made variations, adding a half cup of coconut or nuts (cashews and pecans are good and omit the PB) I have also omitted the PB for allergies sake. This is one of those recipes in which I rarely measure, almost always add extra oats; and only bring the mixture to a rolling boil which funny enough, works out to a minute. Guess what I am trying to say is it is hard to mess up this recipe. For those who have had troubles, the only thing I can think of is perhaps altitude?? Anyway, if they don't work for whatever reason, the cooled batter still tastes good.

I make these all the time as they've become one of my favorite cookies. I use about 1+1/3 cup oatmeal, 1+1/3 cup Fiber One original cereal, and 2/3 cup sliced almonds.  Delicious and satisfying. May try reducing sugar slightly, but they're so good this way.  I find storing these cookies in an air-tight container in the freezer gives them a nice firm consistency and they keep quite a while this way.  Great recipe.

text:
These were good, but did not completely wow me enough for me to give them five stars. Here are some suggestions:
   -Use about 5/8 cup peanut butter, in other words slightly more than a half cup. Crunchy does work best to my preference because with smooth peanut butter it ends up tasting more like dough.
   -Boil 1.5 minutes, stirring constantly, add next set of ingredients quickly, thoroughly stir, then refrigerate for at least 15 minutes. Let cookies sit about 5 minutes at room temp before serving. 
Note*** is okay to use greasing spray such as PAM brand in place of wax paper, but use it sparingly. Enjoy!

Ok, I will bare my soul here. Haha.  I had trouble deciding when to start the timer. I wasn't sure when to declare that it was at the perfect level of "boiling". Anyway, I think I boiled them too long because they looked way too dry.   When I've made them before and they turn out good, the chocolate has a little shine too it and these didn't. I also think I may have added too many oats, because they were too thick to flatten out when they hit the wax paper.    I couldn't serve those, but I had an idea. I started over making a new batch.  Instead of adding 3 cups of oats, I added 1 1/2 cups of oats and 1 1/2 cups of finely crumbled "too dry" cookies from my first attempt.  They turned out great and I didn't have to throw out the first batch!  : )

I'm giving this 5 stars even though mine wouldn't set up.  I think that was due to my ingredients I used.  I used 50% reduced fat margarine, 1 cup Splenda, 1 cup sugar, skim milk.  I used reduced fat smooth peanut butter.  I did bring it to a vigorous boil while constantly stirring and then timed it for 90 seconds.  I had to add about 1 extra cup of oatmeal to even get it to sorta come together.  The taste is fantastic, even if we have to eat in on a plate with a fork.  Yummy chocolatey goodness!  I'm sure with the proper full fat ingredients this would set up fine.

I used to make this recipe and rediscovered it recently.  I especially like the suggestions from "JenniferH" and "Shay"; choose 'view all reviews' and sort by 'most helpful' and theirs will be at the top.  Definitely switch to smooth peanut butter.  Some have said that it doesn't matter if you use regular or quick oats.  I used old-fashioned oats once and it turned out a lot tougher/chewier.  The quick oats are in smaller pieces and give it a much better texture.  I also prefer to use real butter.

text:
These cookies are amazing leave the recipe how it is and it's perfect.  The only problem people seem to have is the boiling time (not enough runny cookies ...too much dry and crumbly)  I'd say for the perfect chewy cookie just boil until your mixture can hold soft peaks in the pot and you should be fine.  In response to Sunflowerr having problems with an oven that doesn't have a high enough cooking temp... most cookies can also be made in the microwave just drop by teaspoon onto waxed paper on microwave oven glass tray. Be sure to make cookies small. Cook about a dozen at a time on full power for 45 to 60 seconds or until firm, but slightly moist. Allow to cool slightly before removing from waxed paper and repeat with remaining dough.

text:
I have made these cookies for years and have discovered that you only have to bring it to a boil, you DO NOT have to boil for a full minute.  All that really has to happen is that the sugar needs to be completely melted.  I also just put the oats and peanut butter in a bowl together and stir them in at the same time, there is no need to melt the peanut butter in the boiled mixture first.  You can also add 1/2 cup coconut flakes, along with the oats.

text:
First of all, these are AWESOME!! I'm not good in the kitchen, and I even managed to make these with no problems at all (a miracle in itself -- didn't even burn the sugar).

Personally, I did use most of the advice in the reviews. I used 4 Tbsp of Hershey's Special Dark cocoa. I did use chunky peanut butter as well (versus smooth as many people suggested). It just added a bit more texture to the whole thing, though they didn't necessarily need it. I also used the recommended 3 1/2 cups of oats (rather than 3).

Definitely read through some of the other reviews for tips! I'd like to try these again, rolling them in coconut maybe!

text:
Quick Tips:
- Use parchment paper. 
- Pre-measure everything to keep things warm and moving. 
- Use a large melon baller to make cookies. This is a life saver. 
- Put the pan back on the off burner while mixing  in the PB to keep the mix warm. 
- Use 3.5c oats if creamy PB.

What I do:
Pre-whisk cocoa and sugar together in other bowl .
Melt butter, then add milk when just melted. 
Add cocoa/sugar right after stirring in milk. 
Heat to rolling boil, then 60 sec boiling. 
Take off heat. 
Add vanilla and salt. 
Add 1/2 cup creamy PB that was pre-measured and ready. I like to stir in the PB while having the pan back on the burner (burner off of course). This keeps it warm. 
Stir in  3 1/2 cups of instant oats, cup at a time. 
Large melon ball scoop makes 33-35 cookies

text:
This basic recipe has been around for ages. I remember making these with my children in their  preschool kitchen way back in the 70's.  Of course, we  Mothers handled the cooking on the stove part,  but  the  kiddos sure loved adding the peanut butter and oats.  I just made these again today,  but used chocolate chips instead of the cocoa powder, so I decreased the butter(never margarine)  to 1/4 cup and sugar to 1 3/4 cup to offset. They turned out wonderful.  I also used the old fashioned rolled oats.     I had to force myself to package them up soon after cooling,  otherwise I would have eaten half the batch myself.

text:
I've been making these for years.  My changes are:  Be sure to bring to a full, rolling boil for 2 full minutes.  I sometimes omit the peanut butter, and instead I add 1 C coconut, 1/2 C chopped pecans, and 1/2 C raisins.  This recipe is very forgiving to changes as long as you boil it properly.   I also avoid making these on rainy days, the extra humidity in the air seems to prevent them from setting properly and then they stay sticky.

I combined this recipe with the other No Bake recipe.  I used 3 good-sized tablespoons of cocoa instead of 1/4 cup (so it was short probably 1 1/2 Teaspoons). They came out great - oh and I omitted the salt (I used salted butter).  These recipes can be tweaked a little, you just have to experiment!

text:
I love No-Bake cookies. For all of you who did not like them, you probably did something wrong. I have been baking for years, and I still miss directions. (everybody does it don't worry)

If your cookies did not firm up and set right, then instead of setting them out on the counter, or where ever else you set them, then freeze them. It takes 1-1 1/2 hours to freeze. If you'd like them to be room temperature, then set them out for 20-30 minutes. They won't melt. They'll hold their shape, and still taste delicious.

If your cookies are too sweet, instead of 2 cups, add one cup of sugar. If they aren't sweet enough, add 1/4 cup sugar, and keep adding 1/4 cup until you like the sweetness.

If they are too dry, add 1-1 1/2 tbsp. milk extra to it. Keep mixing. I would not recommend any more than 2 tbsp. extra milk. 

Thanks yall! I hope this helps!

text:
I've been making these for decades, trying all kinds of variations on it, and had a lot of trial and error with the boiling times. Today, I tried this recipe. The 1 minute boiling time wasn't enough, even with the rolling boil.  I timed it exactly, from a rolling boil (when it doesn't calm down while stirring) and they just didn't ever harden. There's no fixing these cookies if you don't get them right, so I'd rather err on the side of over-boiling than under. 2 minutes  of boiling is better than one, for me anyway.

text:
I've made these a thousand times, exactly as written, and everyone loves them. Two notes: 1) stick with margarine, NOT butter. I know, I'm a butter girl too, but it makes these cookies dry and crumbly. Good ol' Blue Bonnet is the way to go. 2) Once it hits a boil, stick to exactly a minute. The proper temperature is key to it setting up correctly.  Also, if you want to double your batch or if you just like to use a thermometer, bring it up to 220.5 degrees F (104.7 C). Soft but not sticky.

text:
I ALWAYS USE BUTTER! Also, once you put all the ingredients in to heat up in the pot , stir quickly to get the sugar mixed just a bit. Do not stir again until the butter is melting. Minimal stirring is what keeps them from getting dry and crusty. I also let the (creamy) peanut butter sit for a minute once I take it off the heat. Again...once it is heated a bit you don't have to stir so much. They turned out amazing! My husband is my biggest critic and these are his fave cookies! For years I couldn't get them right because I stirred the WHOLE TIME! Am I getting through to you!? Haha! Lastly, I had to set aside my Pampered Chef pan because it (as designed) held in the heat for too long which also made my cookies dry. I use a regular copper bottomed, stainless steel pan and they come out perfect every. stinkin. time.

text:
I had left my recipe on another computer and looked this one up to remember the amounts. I made it almost exactly as written here, except I used smooth peanut butter and dark cocoa and used 3 heaping cups of oatmeal. I returned it to low heat for about 30 seconds while I stirred the oatmeal into the mixture and then removed it from the heat and stirred it until it felt like it was starting to thicken. Then I quickly dropped it onto the waxed paper and placed it in a cool area while they set. They were ready in about 15 minutes. Hub loved them!

text:
These no bakes have been in my family for years. It was the one recipe I knew by heart because I had made them so often. But with kids out of the house do not make them as much.  I had lost my recipe  so I was glad to find it here. The only difference in this recipe from my original one is I use real butter and creamy peanut butter. The place where people mess up the most is how to long cook it.  Cooking it too long they are hard and dry. Too short it doesn't set up. Do not bring this to a rolling boil be gentle with it and it will turn out ever time.

text:
This. Is. The. Recipe.  I cannot say how many times I have attempted this recipe from other sites with complete failure.  From when I was a child and my grandmother first made them, who always got it right, I have not had success on a regular basis -well like 1 in 10 times. This is a cookie I have always loved and would unabashedly beg my friends to make it for me as mine were generally complete flops. However, another reviewer specified the 1 minute rule and that is the key ----to boil the mixture 1 minute after it starts to boil.  Not more, not less. 1 minute.  And I used butter-I won't cook with margarine-but that's just me.  So there you have it.  This is the "cat's meow!"  Be sure to have milk on hand. It will complete the consumption experience perfectly.

I first made these many, many years ago in Home Ec. I recently moved and my recipes are still packed so I found this. It's exactly the same. They were great! The recipe is perfect. For those who had problems with them not firming up or being too crumbly out of the pan, it is an issue of timing. Bring it to a boil for 1 minute. Don't start timing before it boils and don't take too long after.

text:
I made the following tweaks after reading all of the previous reviews: used 3/4 stevia sweetener+3/4 sugar in the raw; almond milk; 1/4 cup margarine (I didn't have butter); 2 teaspoons vanilla; 3 cups of quick oats+ 1 cup shredded coconut flakes; creamy pb; and a pinch of cayenne pepper (gives it a kick and brings out the chocolate flavor). I made sure to boil it at a "rolling boil" for the full minute and have the add-in ingredients ready in a bowl to add as soon as the minute was up.  I added the peanut butter last, per someone's recommendation. Phenomenal!  The only thing I would do differently is to make sure I have crunchy peanut butter on hand, b/c that's how I made it growing up, and I think it really is better than the creamy.

I tried this recipe twice... the first time I didn't boil it long enough because it was too runny coming off the spoon, so I put it all back into the pan for a couple more minutes, got it at the perfect consistency and it came out delicious, perfect no-bake. I thought that the next time I would listen to the instructions and continue boiling for one minute before taking it off the heat, so I did. This time it came out incredibly dry. text:
I've made this recipe about 4 times. I haven't used the crunch peanut butter because we don't use it outside of cooking (in fact, we've never used it in cooking!). 

OK, so compiling the ingredients were fine. But I'm not sure if I agree with atmospheric conditions, outdoor temperatures, whatever the heck other reviewers are saying about home and weather conditions. I followed them to the nines. 

The 1st batch just wouldn't get firm! Not even in the fridge! They were good, and we ate them, but they fell apart. The 2nd time around I added a knife full more peanut butter a spattering more of oats. Still not as firm, but didn't crumble at the mere touch. 3rd time around, I FINALLY figured it out. This recipe (For me) requires a full cup of peanut butter, and about 1/4 cup more oats to become firm. Also, an obvious note, store in the fridge when the cookies harden.

So I rated this recipe 3 stars because the recipe seems to need a little tweaking, but the taste is good.

text:
This recipe works great and has become my go to recipe for no bake cookies.  I do find that butter instead of margarine is key (but some may feel it is a personal preference), and although regular cocoa makes a good tasting cookie, I find that using dutch process cocoa makes for a superb flavor with these.  Only other thing is that I almost never have chunky peanut butter in the house, so use creamy peanut butter in its place.

As for any changes to amounts, I guesstimate on peanut butter - so when I make these the peanut butter may be a little light or a little heavy.  Either way they have turned out good.  

Also with the vanilla, I have used both vanilla extract and vanilla bean paste.  Both give the same results.

text:
I have been making these cookies since I was big enough to reach the stove!  I love this recipe and was so happy to find it on this website.  The only thing I do differently is use real butter instead of margarine, use creamy all natural peanut butter, and I substitute almond milk (unsweetened) for the regular milk.  I have also found that, if you let this come to a full, rolling boil, it takes only one minute to cook after that and they turn out every time.  Another way to test is to take a few drops of the boiling mixture and drip it into a cup of cold water.  If the drops stay together instead of bursting apart, it's done.  Thanks for this wonderful recipe!

text:
I made these for a BBQ, read other users comments, and followed the recipe as written, except that I used real butter.  When I first added PB, oats, and vanilla there was not enough moisture to form cookies, so I put back on the stove top, added another 1/2 to 3/4 cup PB and a few splashes milk, and stirred for about a minute and then dropped on wax paper.  I thought uh-oh, when they immediately became mini oatmeal pancakes, but came back about five minuted later and they were really easy to shape and even held shape when I layered them (with wax paper in between) and place in the refrigerator.  The result was a huge hit, everyone loved them and I will make them again...probably even today!  Might experiment some and see if I can turn it into a healthy breakfast on the go type of a bar.

country:

text:
Exceptional cookies and so easy to make. You can't ask for more.  Only changes I make is I use regular butter instead of margarine and we never buy chunky peanut butter in this house (personal preference) so I always use creamy peanut butter instead.  I've done these so many times and I recently found out a great little trick that I'm not sure if anyone has written it here yet but use an ice cream scoop for these puppies and it will be a breeze! I scoop up the mixture, press it against the plate, get rid of any lingering edges and they plop onto the plate.  I just press them down a little bit to make them more cookie like but it helps take a lot of work out of shaping them. Oh and one last thing, I never boil the mixture for 1 min. I just bring it up to a boil and its off the stove.  I've never had any problems with the cookies shaping or anything like that. Thanks so much for the upload!

The ingredient proportions here are perfect, but the cooking time is off by quite a bit (at least for my stove, at my altitude, etc., etc.). My mother used to make this recipe when I was younger, and now I make it for my kids. The only difference in her recipe and this one is the peanut butter: I use 1/2 cup of creamy (though sometimes I use a little more). I always have all of the ingredients ready before I make this, and I add the peanut butter, then the oats and stir vigorously. These are wonderful and easy enough for children to help you make. My toddler loves to help with these cookies! Just wanted to add that if you don't want to deal with the cocoa powder, you can substitue two one-ounce pouches of Hershey's unsweetened baking chocolate.
